## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress typically increases nonlinearly with strain and decreases with temperature due to thermal softening. Classical constitutive models from plasticity, creep, and thermomechanical coupling are relevant.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear plastic stress-strain curve)
- Hollomon equation with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with exponential thermal effect)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic transition)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 - c4 * T) (saturating hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Arrhenius-type thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Swift law with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal effect)
- Linear thermal softening with hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T) (power hardening times linear thermal factor)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (Taylor expansion of constitutive law)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (sinh-based constitutive model inverted)
- Exponential saturation: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating stress with thermal dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (c0 - c1*T) or exp(-c*T) applied to stress-strain relation
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) forms indicating dislocation density saturation
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with c typically between 0.1 and 0.5 for metals (Hollomon/Ludwik behavior)
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) terms reflecting Boltzmann statistics in dislocation motion
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield strength before hardening: sigma = c0 + f(epsilon)
- Competing hardening and softening → Product structure f(epsilon) * g(T) separating strain hardening from thermal softening
- Phase transformation effects → Sigmoidal dependence on temperature near transition: terms like 1/(1+exp(c*(T-T_c)))
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Sum of linear and nonlinear terms: c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**c2 capturing regime change
